Well Evaluation
Marathon Oil Company
Kerkhoff 14-8H
Figure 1. Ensign #161 drilling the Kerkhoff 14-8H, November 2014
INTRODUCTION
The Marathon Oil Company Kerkhoff 14-8H well is located approximately 7 miles northwest of
Manning in Dunn County, North Dakota [NW NW Section 17, T144N, R96W]. The Kerkhoff
14-8H is a single lateral, double section horizontal well that's part of a multi-well pad, and has a
target pay zone in the Mississippian-Devonian Middle Bakken Member. The Middle Bakken is
known as a mixed carbonate-clastic sequence stratigraphically sequenced between two
petroliferous, carbonaceous black shales, the Upper Bakken Shale and the Lower Bakken Shale.
The two shales combined serve as the prospects source rock.
PLAN
The drilling plan stipulated that the vertical hole inclination should be held at an inclination of
2.50º with an azimuth of 320° from surface casing, at 2,300', until approximately 10,367' MD
where the curve would be kicked-off for a 12º per 100' build rate until landing at approximately
11,320' MD (10,891' TVD) into the Middle Bakken target. Prognosis estimated the landing
target to be 15' below the base of the upper Bakken shale. After landing, intermediate casing
would then be set and cemented to isolate the target reservoir, and the lateral would commence.
The lateral would continue north at approximately 354.79º to a bottom hole location within Lot 4
of Section 5, T144N-R96W.
OFFSET CONTROL
Top and thickness control was provided by multiple offset wells. The following offset wells
provided gamma signatures to correlate formation tops and determine a proper target landing.
The MOC Louie Hendricks 24-20H. The wellhead is located approximately 2
miles south of the subject well, and it was a horizontal Middle Bakken well
drilled in June of 2009.
The Davis Oil Co. Murphy Creek State 1 is located approximately 1.3 miles
east of the Kerkhoff 14-8H, and was completed in December of 1983. The
Murphy Creek State 1 was a vertical hole drilled down to the Duperow
formation, and is classified as a dry hole. This offset is used to land the well
and provide an entire Middle Bakken gamma signature.
The MOC Piatt 11-17H shares a pad with the subject well. The Piatt 11-17H
curve was landed on September 25th 2014. It provides our closest offset and its
gamma signature was used to aid in a precise Middle Bakken curve landing.
Additional data from the Ivan Hecker 41-6H and Hazel 14-8H also provided gamma signature
and structure control during lateral operations (Figure 2).
ENGINEERING
The well was spud by rig Ensign #161 on September 12, 2014. Surface casing was set using 9
5/8" 36 pound J-55 casing, which isolated the surface hole to 2,300' MD. Here the rig was skid
to continue surface, batch drilling operations.
On September 27th, 2014, the remaining vertical hole commenced with diesel invert drilling fluid
with a weight of 9.6 - 10.6 ppg. The vertical was drilled with two assemblies to a kick-off point
of 10,160' MD. The curve was kicked off at 10,160' MD, using a 2.12° mud motor, and
completed at 11,325' MD (10,896' TVD). The curve section reached landing point in
approximately 21 hours, using one bit and three separate assembly arrangements.
After
completing the curve section of the well, 7" casing was set and cemented to 11,310' MD, using
32# P-110 casing. Here the rig was skid to continue vertical-curve, batch drilling operations.
On November 30th, 2014, in preparation for drilling the lateral portion of the well, invert diesel
drilling fluid was displaced with saltwater drilling fluid. A single BHA using a 6" PDC bit and
BHI, XLP motor was used to drill the entire lateral section from 11,325' to 21,670' MD in 74.2
hours.
The Kerkhoff 14-8H reached a total depth of 21,670' on December 4th, 2014, at a closure
direction of 355.17° and a true vertical depth (TVD) of 10,945'. The bottom hole location is
estimated to be 10,942.53' north & 924.03' west of the surface location or approximately 208.71'
FNL & 76.97' FWL, Lot 4 Section 5, T144N, R96W (Figure 2).

GEOLOGIC EVALUATION
Methods
A two-person geology team logged drill cuttings, monitored mud gas and provided guidance for
steering. Sample and gas evaluation began in the Amsden Formation at 8,000' MD. Rig crew
members caught 30' lagged samples under direction of the well-site geologists. Wet and dry
cuttings were examined under a binocular microscope. Two sets of dry cuttings were collected
and sent to Marathon Oil Company and the North Dakota Geological Survey. A digital gas
detector (total gas with chromatograph) was interfaced with a Pason electronic data recorder
(EDR). The Pason EDR provided hole depth, bit depth and pump stroke information to the gas
detection program (MController) and distributed the detector's total gas information for viewing
across location. Total mud gas was recorded in units (100 units = 1% methane equivalent in air)
and chromatography of C1 ­ C4 components were calculated in parts-per-million.
Lithology
Note: There were no electric logs run for the Kerkhoff 14-8H; therefore, all depths while drilling the vertical and
curve are referenced to driller's depth.
Beginning in the Amsden Formation, sample logging continued into the Mississippian-Devonian
Middle Bakken Member. Sampling began in the Amsden Formation in response to observed
higher gas values in a previous vertical on the same pad. No zones of porosity were observed,
though lithological and gas data can be found in the vertical logs. The Bakken Formation is the
only lithology discussed in detail here, complete sample descriptions by depth can be found in an
addendum to this report.
The Bakken Formation, Upper Bakken Shale Member was penetrated at 10,858' TVD (-8,737'
MSL). This member is easily recognized by a sharp increase and sustained high gamma ray
counts, a marked increase in penetration rates, and typically sustained higher gas shows. The
upper member is a distinct black, petroliferous & carbonaceous shale containing occasional to
common disseminated and nodular pyrite (Figure 3). The Middle Bakken Member was
penetrated at 10,871' TVD (-8,450' MSL). The middle member consists of a siltstone, limestone
and silty sandstone. The target zone consists of light to medium gray-brown silty sandstone,
containing fine intergranular porosity and light spotty to even brown oil staining (Figure 4).
Figures 3 & 4: Cuttings of the Bakken Fm., upper shale (left), and middle member silty sandstone (right).
Geosteering
The well prognosis called for a landing target 15' into the Middle Bakken Member, at a depth of
10,891' TVD. Using gamma signatures from offset wells, well-site geologists were able to
correlate formation tops in order to make any necessary corrections to the prognosis landing
target. Lodgepole markers came in consistently high to prognosis, and the decision was made to
raise the landing target a total of 5' to 10,886' TVD. The actual curve landing came in at 10,896'
TVD due to poor build rates, landing the well-bore 6' below the base of our 8' geologic window.
Three primary gamma signatures were used to steer the well in an 8' thick geologic window.
Throughout our target interval, gamma counts ranged from roughly 40-95 API, and oscillated
with regularity. This gamma trend was pervasive throughout our entire zone which proposed a
challenge determining our precise location in target, within the laminated facies. Two other
primary markers were observed above and below our target zone. Above the zone, a reliable
packestone layer, gamma marker was observed. Gamma counts in this packestone layer
registered considerably lower, to around 20-30 (API), though oscillation between these cooler
gamma counts and hotter counts up to 115 (API) were also observed, indicating possible laminar
limestone deposition. At the bottom of our target interval, a hotter and tighter gamma marker
was observed with (API) counts of 85-95. This marker bounded our target zone below and was
encountered once during the lateral. These markers provided data upon which formation dip was
calculated, and were consistent throughout the lateral.
The target window in the Middle Bakken was entered at approximately 11,140' MD, and the
well-bore was maintained in the target for approximately 80% of the lateral. Over the course of
the 10,530' exposure to the middle member, structure dropped a total of 62.70' TVD, resulting in
a gross apparent dip of -0.34° (Figure 5).

Hydrocarbons
A slight increase in gas values were observed near the bottom of the Lodgepole Formation.
Several gas shows, between 500 & 1,500 units, were observed while drilling the curve through
the lower Lodgepole, False Bakken, and Upper Bakken Shale Member. These shows can most
likely be attributed to high hydrocarbon content in the Upper Bakken Shale, as well as zones of
possible fracture porosity towards the bottom of the Lodgepole Formation.
Background gas throughout the lateral ranged from 250 - 3,000 units, with an average of around
2,200 units. Several intervals of the lateral produced notable increases in background gas and gas
shows. The highest gas shows were observed while the wellbore drilled towards the top of our
target window, however apart from this observation, there is little evidence to link high gas
shows to a particular portion of our drilling window. Observed increases are likely a result of
localized zones of high porosity, overpressure or possible fracture porosity.
Oil was observed coming over the shakers early in the lateral, changing from light brown to
brown-red as the lateral progressed. Spotty to even brown oil staining was observed in sample
for the entire duration of the lateral, and fluorescent cuts of samples yielded primarily moderate
to fast streaming green-blue cuts.
Gas was vented through the gas buster beginning at 12,000' MD, and circulated through the gas
buster beginning at 13,982' MD and continuing throughout the remainder of the lateral. A 3-5'
intermittent flare was observed beginning around 13,500' MD, occasionally increasing to around
5-10'. Gas values increased notably after total depth while liner was run, with gas shows over
8,500 units and associated 30-40' flares. No back-pressure was held during the well (Figure 6).

SUMMARY
The Marathon Oil Company, Kerkhoff 14-8H was drilled in 18 days, reaching a total depth of
21,670' MD on December 4th, 2014. An extended sampling program, beginning in the Amsden
Formation and logging the entire Tyler Formation, was performed to investigate possible zones
of porosity indicated by increased gas shows observed in wells that share a pad with the subject
well. No evidence was found indicating zones of further interest. The lateral portion of the well
exposed 10,530' of the Middle Bakken Member, and was determined to be 80% within the target
interval. Samples from the Middle Bakken consisted of light to medium gray-brown silty
sandstone with intergranular porosity and light, spotty brown oil staining. An overall dip of -
0.34° was calculated using a combination of gamma ray, sample analysis, and drilling parameter
data. Despite the challenges presented by the lack of reliable gamma markers directly within our
target interval and relatively thin Middle Bakken interval, the well proved to be an engineering
and geologic success. Sample analyses combined with gas data provide strong evidence that the
Kerkhoff 14-8H will be a successful Middle Bakken well. The project currently awaits fracture
stimulation to maximize its full potential as an oil and gas well.
Respectfully submitted,
Nathan Stansfield
Anna Bruckmeier
Sunburst Consulting, Inc.

LITHOLOGY
Marathon Oil Company ­ Kerkhoff 14-8H
Rig crews caught lagged samples in 30' intervals under the supervision of Sunburst geologists. A
detailed list of sampling intervals is included in the well data summary page. Sample or gamma ray
marker tops have been inserted in the sample descriptions below for reference. Samples were examined
wet and dry under a binocular microscope. The drilling fluid was diesel based invert from surface casing
to 11,310' and changed to salt-water from 11,310' to 21,670' (TD). Sample collection began at 8,000'.
Drilling in the Amsden Formation

gray-brown, microcrystalline, friable, earthy to chalky texture, calcareous in part, no visible porosity; common
ANHYDRITE: off white to cream, soft, amorphous

Dear Natalie:
Pursuant to Commission Order No. 22900, approval to drill the above captioned well is hereby given. The
approval is granted on the condition that all portions of the well bore not isolated by cement, shall be located
approximately down the north-south axis (500' drilling corridor per Commission policy) and be no closer than the 200'
setback from the north & south boundaries within the 2560 acre spacing unit consisting of Sections 5, 6, 7 & 8 T144N
R96W.
PERMIT STIPULATIONS: In cases where a spacing unit is accessed from an off-site drill pad, an affidavit
must be provided affirming that the surface owner of the multi-well pad agrees to accept burial on their
property of the cuttings generated from drilling the well(s) into an offsite spacing/drilling unit. Effective
June 1, 2014, a covered leak-proof container (with placard) for filter sock disposal must be maintained on the
well site beginning when the well is spud, and must remain on-site during clean-out, completion, and flow-
back whenever filtration operations are conducted. Marathon may set conductor on permitted wells only.
MARATHON OIL CO must contact NDIC Field Inspector Nicole Nelson at 701-290-1527 prior to location
construction.
Drilling pit
NDAC 43-02-03-19.4 states that "a pit may be utilized to bury drill cuttings and solids generated during well drilling
and completion operations, providing the pit can be constructed, used and reclaimed in a manner that will prevent
pollution of the land surface and freshwaters. Reserve and circulation of mud system through earthen pits are
prohibited. All pits shall be inspected by an authorized representative of the director prior to lining and use. Drill
cuttings and solids must be stabilized in a manner approved by the director prior to placement in a cuttings pit."
Form 1 Changes & Hard Lines
Any changes, shortening of casing point or lengthening at Total Depth must have prior approval by the NDIC. The
proposed directional plan is at a legal location. The minimum legal coordinate from the well head at casing point is:
. Also, based on the azimuth of the proposed lateral the maximum legal coordinate from the well head is:
.
Location Construction Commencement (Three Day Waiting Period)
Operators shall not commence operations on a drill site until the 3rd business day following publication of the
approved drilling permit on the NDIC - OGD Daily Activity Report. If circumstances require operations to
commence before the 3rd business day following publication on the Daily Activity Report, the waiting period may be
waived by the Director. Application for a waiver must be by sworn affidavit providing the information necessary to
evaluate the extenuating circumstances, the factors of NDAC 43-02-03-16.2 (1), (a)-(f), and any other information that
would allow the Director to conclude that in the event another owner seeks revocation of the drilling permit, the
applicant should retain the permit.
Natalie Menge

Permit Fee & Notification
Payment was received in the amount of $100 via credit card. It is requested that notification be given
immediately upon the spudding of the well. This information should be relayed to the Oil & Gas Division, Bismarck,
via telephone. The following information must be included: Well name, legal location, permit number, drilling
contractor, company representative, date and time of spudding. Office hours are 8:00 a.m. to 12:00 p.m. and 1:00 p.m.
to 5:00 p.m. Central Time. Our telephone number is (701) 328-8020, leave a message if after hours or on the weekend.
Survey Requirements for Horizontal, Horizontal Re-entry, and Directional Wells
NDAC Section 43-02-03-25 (Deviation Tests and Directional Surveys) states in part (that) the survey contractor
shall file a certified copy of all surveys with the director free of charge within thirty days of completion. Surveys must
be submitted as one electronic copy, or in a form approved by the director. However, the director may require the
directional survey to be filed immediately after completion if the survey is needed to conduct the operation of the
director's office in a timely manner. Certified surveys must be submitted via email in one adobe document, with a
certification cover page to certsurvey@nd.gov.
Survey points shall be of such frequency to accurately determine the entire location of the well bore.
Specifically, the Horizontal and Directional well survey frequency is 100 feet in the vertical, 30 feet in the curve (or
when sliding) and 90 feet in the lateral.
Confidential status
Your request for confidential status of all information furnished to the Director, or his representatives, is hereby
granted. Such information, except production runs, shall remain confidential for six months commencing on the date
the well is spud.
Confidential status notwithstanding, the Director and his representatives shall have access to all well records
wherever located. Your company personnel, or any person performing work for your company shall permit the
Director and his representatives to come upon any lease, property, well, or drilling rig operated or controlled by them,
complying with all safety rules, and to inspect the records and operation of such wells and to have access at all times to
any and all records of wells. The Commission's field personnel periodically inspect producing and drilling wells. Any
information regarding such wells shall be made available to them at any time upon request. The information so
obtained by the field personnel shall be maintained in strict confidence and shall be available only to the Commission
and its staff.
Surface casing cement
Tail cement utilized on surface casing must have a minimum compressive strength of 500 psi within 12 hours,
and tail cement utilized on production casing must have a minimum compressive strength of 500 psi before drilling the
plug or initiating tests.
Logs
NDAC Section 43-02-03-31 requires the running of (1) a suite of open hole logs from which formation tops and
porosity zones can be determined, (2) a Gamma Ray Log run from total depth to ground level elevation of the well
bore, and (3) a log from which the presence and quality of cement can be determined (Standard CBL or Ultrasonic
cement evaluation log) in every well in which production or intermediate casing has been set, this log must be run prior
to completing the well. All logs run must be submitted free of charge, as one digital TIFF (tagged image file format)
copy and one digital LAS (log ASCII) formatted copy. Digital logs may be submitted on a standard CD, DVD, or
attached to an email sent to digitallogs@nd.gov Thank you for your cooperation.

April 9, 2014
RE:
Filter Socks and Other Filter Media
Leakproof Container Required
Oil and Gas Wells
Dear Operator,
North Dakota Administrative Code Section 43-02-03-19.2 states in part that all waste material associated with
exploration or production of oil and gas must be properly disposed of in an authorized facility in accord with all
applicable local, state, and federal laws and regulations.
Filtration systems are commonly used during oil and gas operations in North Dakota. The Commission is very
concerned about the proper disposal of used filters (including filter socks) used by the oil and gas industry.
Effective June 1, 2014, a container must be maintained on each well drilled in North Dakota beginning when the
well is spud and must remain on-site during clean-out, completion, and flow-back whenever filtration operations
are conducted. The on-site container must be used to store filters until they can be properly disposed of in an
authorized facility. Such containers must be:
leakproof to prevent any fluids from escaping the container
covered to prevent precipitation from entering the container
placard to indicate only filters are to be placed in the container
If the operator will not utilize a filtration system, a waiver to the container requirement will be considered, but
only upon the operator submitting a Sundry Notice (Form 4) justifying their request.
As previously stated in our March 13, 2014 letter, North Dakota Administrative Code Section 33-20-02.1-01
states in part that every person who transports solid waste (which includes oil and gas exploration and production
wastes) is required to have a valid permit issued by the North Dakota Department of Health, Division of Waste
Management. Please contact the Division of Waste Management at (701) 328-5166 with any questions on the
solid waste program. Note oil and gas exploration and production wastes include produced water, drilling mud,
invert mud, tank bottom sediment, pipe scale, filters, and fly ash.
Thank you for your cooperation.
Sincerely,
Bruce E. Hicks
Assistant Director
Marathon Oil Company

1.
BOP EQUIPMENT
Marathon Oil Company's minimum specifications for pressure
control equipment are as follows:
Ram Type:
13 5/8" 5000 psi blind, pipe and annular.
a. Due to Marathon's experience it is felt that the above
referenced BOP equipment is adequate for drilling this well.
The reduced permeability of the target zone along with
Marathon's area experience of drilling over 250 horizontal
wells indicate that a MASP of 3000 psi is more adjusted to
the reality of the reservoir.
BOP and other equipment testing:
a. Floor valve, dart valve, kill valves, check valve, manual
choke line valve, manual top drive valve, hydraulic top
drive valve, HCR, choke house valves, choke manifold,
choke hose, choke line, kill line, upper pipe rams, lower
pipe rams, blind rams (Low Test: 250 psi x 5 min. High
Test: 5000 psi x 10 min.)
b. Annular Preventer (Low Test: 250 psi x 5 min. High Test:
2500 psi x 10 min.)
c. Rotating head and Orbit Valve (Low Test: 250 psi x 5 min.
High Test: 1500 psi x 10 min.)
Frequency:
a. After initial installation (NU BOPE).
b. Whenever any seal subject to test pressure is broken.
c. After any repairs compromising seal.
d. At 30-day intervals.
All other equipment (upper and lower Kelly cocks, IBOP,
etc) will be tested according to Onshore Oil and Gas
Order No. 2.

d. Pursuant to NDIC letter effective February 12,2014,
concerning Hydraulic Fracture Stimulation using Diesel
Fuels, Marathon Oil Company will not inject diesel fuel
or any diesel-type chemicals (68334-30-5, 68476-34-6,
68476-30-2, 68476-31-3, or 8008-20-6) during the
hydraulic fracture stimulation process or this well.
Marathon understands the guidelines that are outline in
the above referenced letter including the requirement to
obtain an Underground Injection Control, Class II permit
from the NDIC prior to commencing any Hydraulic Fracture
Stimulation in which any amount of diesel fuel or any
diesel type chemical is injected.

SUNDRY NOTICES AND REPORTS ON WELLS - FORM 4
SFN 5749
1. Approval shall be obtained prior to perforating or recompleting a well in a reservoir other than the
reservoir in which the well is currently completed, prior to plug back of a well, prior to temporary
abandonment of a well, prior to abandonment of a well, prior to reclamation of a well site, prior to
reclamation of a reserve pit, and prior to beginning a workover project, which may qualify for a tax
exemption pursuant to NDCC Section 57-51.1-03. Please refer to Section 43-02-03-16 of the
North Dakota Administrative Code (NDAC) regarding recompleting a well in a reservoir other than
the reservoir in which the well is currently completed or plugging back of a well, to Section 43-02-
03-55 NDAC regarding temporary abandonment of a well, to Section 43-02-03-33 or Section 43-
02-05-08 NDAC regarding abandonment of wells, to Section 43-02-03-19 NDAC regarding
reclamation, and to Section 43-02-09-03 NDAC regarding workover projects.
2. Upon the completion of any remedial work, or attempted remedial work such as plugging back,
drilling deeper, acidizing, shooting, formation fracturing, squeezing operations, setting liner, fishing
operations, repair work, perforating, reperforating, or other similar operations not specifically
covered herein, a report on the operation shall be filed on a Sundry Notice - Form 4 (SFN 5749)
with the Director. The report shall present a detailed account of all work done and the date of
such work; the daily production of oil, gas, and water both prior to and after the operation; the
shots per foot, size, and depth of perforations; the quantity of sand, crude, chemical, or other
materials employed in the operation; and any other pertinent information or operations which
affect the original status of the well and are not specifically covered herein. Please refer to
Section 43-02-03-31 NDAC.
3. Upon the completion of a workover project, which may qualify for a tax exemption pursuant to
NDCC Section 57-51.1-03, a report on the operation shall be filed on a Sundry Notice - Form 4
(SFN 5749) detailing the work done. Include the dates during which the workover rig was in
service actually performing work on the workover project and the date the workover was
completed, a detailed list identifying all labor, services, and materials used and equipment
replaced during the workover project, the cost of each item, and whether the replacement
equipment was new or used. The value of all equipment removed from service must be listed.
The average daily oil production from the well during the first two months after completion of the
project must be included if the costs of the project did not exceed sixty-five thousand dollars. All
gauge tickets of oil produced in incomplete months during the first two months after completion of
the workover and the volume of oil stored on the well premises immediately prior to
commencement of the workover project must also be included. Please refer to Section 43-02-09-
04 NDAC.
4. Upon the initial installation of pumping equipment, or change in type or depth of pumping
equipment designed to increase productivity in a well, the operator shall file a Sundry Notice -
Form 4 (SFN 5749) of such installation. The notice shall include all pertinent information on the
pump and the operation thereof including the date of such installation, and the daily production of
the well prior to and after the pump has been installed. Please refer to Section 43-02-03-31
NDAC.
5. The well file number, well name and number, well location, field, pool, and county shall coincide
with the official records on file with the Commission.
6. The original and one copy of this report shall be filed with the Industrial Commission of North
Dakota, Oil and Gas Division, 600 East Boulevard, Dept. 405, Bismarck, ND 58505-0840.
